SUBJECT:
Charter Amendments – Public Hearing
RECOMMENDATION:
Hold a public hearing regarding proposed City Charter amendments addressing how the Mayor is chosen, how vacancies 
on the City Council are filled, district elections, and other revisions; and provide direction on how to group proposed 
amendments between two separate ballot measures.
BACKGROUND:
At its Fiscal Year 2022-23 Goal Setting, the City Council directed staff to review and update the City Charter related to 
district elections, mayoral rotation, and filling Council vacancies. In addition, staff is proposing other miscellaneous 
changes to the Charter where warranted, in the interests of removing or modifying outdated language. This is explained 
later in this report.  After holding a study session on July 17, 2023 regarding board and commission qualifications and 
compensation, the Council held further study sessions on October 16, 2023, January 2, 2024, and March 4, 2024 to go over 
proposed Charter amendment language.  Each of the agreed-upon revisions are described below, and the full text is 
included as Attachment 1.  The explanations that follow each proposed amendment are largely from prior study session 
staff reports that addressed these topics.  
As noted during the March 4, 2024 study session, at a future meeting staff will ask the City Council whether to place 
Charter amendments on the ballot in November 2024 or November 2026.  The potential complication is that another 
ballot measure is also likely to be placed on the ballot in November 2024, in the form of an amendment to Measure Y.  
Once polling information is provided by the City’s consultants, staff anticipates returning to the Council with this question 
at the May 20, 2024 meeting.
DISCUSSION:
As previously discussed, staff recommends that amendments should be divided into two separate ballot measures. One 
would include changes that reflect the shift to district elections, remove outdated language, or are otherwise non-
controversial. The remaining amendments would be included in a separate measure, which are addressed first in this 
report.  The following discussion organizes proposed amendments into two different groups, corresponding to two 
separate measures, as proposed by staff.
PROPOSED BALLOT MEASURE NO. 1
A.   Filling Council Vacancies  
238 of 269

--- page 239 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Existing Charter Language (Sec. 2.08)
Proposed Charter Language
 
A vacancy on the city council from whatever cause arising 
shall be filled by appointment by the council provided, 
that if the council fails to agree or for any other reason 
does not fill such vacancy within 30 days after the same 
occurs, then such vacancy shall be filled by the mayor. The 
appointee shall hold office until the next general election, 
when a successor shall be chosen by the electors for the 
unexpired term. If for any reason the seats of a majority of 
the council become vacant, then the city clerk shall call a 
special election at once to fill the vacancies for the 
unexpired terms, and the same shall be conducted 
substantially in the manner provided for general municipal 
elections. The candidates receiving the most votes shall 
serve the longer, if any, of the unexpired terms, and in 
case of ties the terms shall be fixed by lot.  
 
 
A vacancy on the city council from whatever cause arising 
shall be filled by appointment by the council provided, 
that if the council fails to agree or for any other reason 
does not fill such vacancy within 30 60 days after the same 
occurs, then the city clerk shall call a special election at 
once to fill such vacancy such vacancy shall be filled by 
the mayor. The An appointee shall hold office until the 
next general election, when a successor shall be chosen by 
the electors for the unexpired term. If for any reason the 
seats of a majority of the council become vacant, then the 
city clerk shall call a special election at once to fill the 
vacancies for the unexpired terms, and the same shall be 
conducted substantially in the manner provided for 
general municipal elections. The candidates receiving the 
most votes shall serve the longer, if any, of the unexpired 
terms, and in case of ties the terms shall be fixed by lot.
By replacing the phrase, “the mayor” with text calling for a special election, the draft wording would remove the authority 
of the Mayor to fill vacancies and instead send the decision to the voters, if the Council is unable to decide within the 
allotted time. Notably, in 1983 Measure C was submitted to the voters that would have accomplished the same purpose 
with somewhat different wording, but that measure failed by a 46.4% to 53.6% vote.  
 
The time for the Council to decide on filling a vacancy would also be increased from 30 to 60 days. This is important 
because if a vacancy occurs due to a Councilmember being elected to another office, that will likely occur in November. 
The existing 30-day period would then expire in December during the holiday season. Extending the period to 60 days 
would allow for increased outreach to the community and a more deliberate application, interview, and selection process. 
The Council would also have more time to weigh the benefits and drawbacks (such as expense) of a special election, versus 
deciding to fill the vacancy after extensive community input. 
 
Finally, the draft language eliminates text allowing candidates receiving the most votes to serve the longer of unexpired 
terms (and addressing tie votes) where a majority of the Council seats become vacant.  Following the shift to district 
elections, candidates would no longer run for one of several at-large seats and would instead run for a single seat in their 
district.  Thus, the current language is no longer necessary.

purposes. The council may, in its discretion, change the

CITY OF SAN MATEO
date of any regularly scheduled Monday council meeting 
which would fall on a holiday or other inconvenient day to 
the nearest convenient day subsequent to the regularly

(b)  The selection of the mayor and deputy mayor shall

shall be selected as deputy mayor.  Except however, a

(c)  The regular meetings of the council shall be held on

inconvenient day to the nearest convenient day 
subsequent to the regularly scheduled Monday council

The proposed language would remove 6:30 p.m. as the start time for Council meetings and simply allow the time to be 
determined by resolution.  Note this represents a change from prior draft language that referenced an ordinance, because 
a resolution will provide the Council with more flexibility.  
Regarding the mayoral rotation, the proposed language would address both the procedure and substance of selecting a 
mayor and deputy mayor.  First, as previously proposed, it would require the Council to select a Mayor at the first regular 
meeting in December and would prohibit continuing the action to a future date, as specified.  But additional changes are 
proposed to codify the key aspects of the Council Guidelines, namely to frame the process of selecting a Mayor and 
Deputy Mayor as a ministerial act by strictly following a rotational sequence.  In order to avoid a lengthy Charter section, 
the proposed language states that the details are to be specified in an ordinance.  The ordinance would generally include 
the following provisions from the Council Guidelines:  
1.
After serving as mayor, that council member moves to the end of the rotation sequence, and the other four 
council members move forward.  
2.
When a council member is newly elected or appointed (as the result of a cancelled election), that new council 
member goes into the fourth position in the rotation, after all incumbents, but before the current outgoing Mayor.  
3.
If two or more council members are newly elected or appointed at the same time, the newly elected or appointed 
council members shall draw lots to determine their position relative to one another in the rotational sequence. 
4.
If a council member is appointed to fill a mid-term vacancy, that council member will go to the bottom of the 
rotational list.  
5.
Incumbent council members, when re-elected, do not begin anew at the bottom of the list, but rather retain their 
placement in the rotation.  
6.
If for any reason, such as death, resignation, recall, or not seeking re-election, a council member is removed from 
the rotation, the remaining council members move forward in the sequence.  
Chapter 5 of the Council Guidelines contains the current policy and can be found here.

This language would allow non-citizens to serve on boards and commissions, such as lawful permanent residents.  It would 
also require board and commission members to be City residents at least 18 years of age, consistent with Senate Bill 225 
(2019).  At the March 4, 2024 study session, the City Council elected to not pursue Charter amendments that would have 
allowed non-residents to serve and would have allowed compensation for members of boards and commissions.  The 
portion of Section 6.05 proposed to be amended is shown in the chart above, and the full text is set forth in Attachment 1.  
PROPOSED BALLOT MEASURE NO. 2
The draft Charter amendments in this measure would consist of changes reflecting the switch to district elections and 
other non-controversial revisions, as shown below.  
A.  District Elections
Existing Charter Language (Sec. 2.01(a))
Proposed Charter Language
There shall be a city council of five members elected by 
the voters of the city at large.  
There shall be a city council of five members elected by 
the voters of the city at large by districts.  Any recall 
election or special election or appointment to fill a 
vacancy shall also be by district.  Following each 
decennial federal census, and at other such times as 
provided by law, the city council shall, by ordinance, 
adopt boundaries for all council districts so that all of 
the districts shall comply with state and federal law.
The members of the Council are now elected by district rather than at large, following a 2021 demand letter claiming a 
violation of the California Voting Rights Act and a change in City electoral practices. The district election process is also 
codified in the San Mateo Municipal Code. The additional proposed language clarifies that a redistricting process will occur 
every ten years, consistent with state and federal law, and that an appointee to fill a vacancy must live in the same district 
as the Councilmember who vacated the seat at issue.

This Charter provision was added by the voters in 2017 in order to comply with Senate Bill 415 (SB 415) (2015). SB 415 
required cities to realign their elections to even numbered years if prior odd-year elections had resulted in a significant 
decrease in voter turnout. The City’s 2017 ballot measure did so, also extending the terms of Council members elected in 
2015 and 2017 by one year to facilitate this goal. It passed by a vote 81.4% to 18.6%. However, the terms of office for 
Council members elected in 2015 and 2017 have now ended (as of 2022 for the latter), and this language is no longer 
needed. Charter Section 2.01(c) provides for the staggered election of Councilmembers in 2020 (two seats) and 2022 
(three seats), and even-numbered years thereafter, for a term of four years.

Any ordinance declared by the council to be

Any ordinance declared by the council to be 
necessary as an emergency measure for preserving 
the public peace, health, safety, or welfare and

242 of 269

--- page 243 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
The draft language would allow for the publication of a summary of an emergency ordinance (more commonly known as
an urgency ordinance). Currently, the Charter does not allow publication of a summary, and therefore the entire urgency 
ordinance must be published in the newspaper. This change would result in modest cost savings, but more importantly 
would allow for the same flexibility in publishing urgency ordinances that exists for standard ordinances under Charter 
Section 2.15(d).
Furthermore, this proposal would eliminate language requiring the automatic repeal of urgency ordinances on the 91st day
after adoption. This language was not part of the original 1922 Charter and was added in 1970. The circumstances
requiring the urgency ordinance would not necessarily have been resolved approximately three months after adoption.
Eliminating this text would not prevent the Council from affirmatively repealing an urgency ordinance as appropriate.

The language proposed for elimination originally appeared in the 1922 Charter and has only undergone minor changes 
over the years.  As the Council is well aware, the manner in which election campaigns are conducted has vastly changed 
over the last century.  Instead of a statement with the prescribed information constituting a significant source of 
information for the voters, other sources of information are much more commonly used during an election campaign, such 
as Internet websites with written material and videos, social media, and other sources.  Candidates may also submit a 
statement to be included in a voter information guide that is distributed to voters.  This existing provision is thus outdated 
and is appropriate for removal, subject to voter approval.  
E.  Miscellaneous Charter Revisions
Staff is also proposing miscellaneous “clean-up” revisions to the Charter, namely adding gender neutral language where 
needed, lettering paragraphs and adding commas where appropriate, and correcting a typo (in Section 9.07 where 
“within” was inadvertently separated into two words).  The full text of proposed Charter Amendments is set forth in 
Attachment 1.  
CHARTER AMENDMENT PROCESS
Under state law, the City Council may propose a charter amendment and submit it to the voters at the next statewide 
general election, at least 88 days before the election. Govt. §34458(a). The charter amendment will not be adopted until
it is approved by a majority vote.
244 of 269

--- page 245 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Before approving the submittal of a charter amendment to the voters, the City Council must hold at least two public 
hearings, with published and posted notice, at least 21 calendar days prior to the date of each public hearing. Govt. 
§34458(b). Tonight is the first public hearing.  
The second public hearing must be held at least 30 days after the first public hearing, and at least one of the two hearings 
must be held outside of normal business hours to facilitate public participation. Govt. §34458(b). The Council cannot vote 
on whether to approve submitting the proposal to the voters until 21 days after the second public hearing. Govt. 
§34458(b). The Charter amendment must also be filed with the California Secretary of State and must be published in the 
official state statutes. Govt. §34461. 
Below is the schedule that builds in a buffer between the projected date of submittal to the voters and the statutory 
deadline of 88 days before the election. This will allow for better coordination with the County Elections office and an 
additional Council meeting, if necessary.
Council Meeting Schedule – Charter Amendments

As noted at the outset of this report, it is possible that the Charter amendments may be put before the voters in 
November 2026 rather than November 2024, subject to direction from the City Council.  Staff anticipates returning to the 
Council to receive direction on May 20, 2024 in connection with the results of polling activities by the City’s consultants.  
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact associated with this study session. Should the Council direct staff to pursue further action on 
charter amendments, further analysis and scoping will be required. Hiring a ballot measure consultant and polling 
consultant will likely cost approximately $52,300. Note that consistent with state law, no public funds can be used to 
advocate for or against a ballot measure. Instead, these funds would be used for polling and education and information to 
determine how each measure should be formulated. Finally, placing each measure on the ballot at the consolidated 
November 5, 2024 election will also cost approximately $100,000.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This public hearing is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
Before approving the submittal of a charter amendment to the voters, the City Council must hold at least two public 
hearings, with published and posted notice, at least 21 calendar days prior to the date of each public hearing. Govt. 
§34458(b). The public hearing notice was published on March 8, 2024  in the San Mateo Daily Journal.  
The second public hearing must be held at least 30 days after the first public hearing, and at least one of the two hearings 
must be held outside of normal business hours to facilitate public participation. Govt. §34458(b).  The second public 
hearing is scheduled for May 6, 2024.  Both hearings will be held outside of normal business hours, during regular 
meetings of the City Council starting at 7:00 p.m.

San Mateo City Charter
ARTICLE I NAME, BOUNDARIES, AND POWERS OF THE CITY
1.01
Name of The City.
The municipal corporation now existing and known as the City of San Mateo shall remain and continue 
to be a body politic and corporate as at present, in name, in fact and in law.
1.02
Boundaries.
The boundaries of said city shall be the same as now established, with power and authority to change 
the same as provided by law.
1.03
Powers.
Said city, by and through its council and other officials, shall have, and may exercise, all powers 
necessary or appropriate to a municipal corporation and the general welfare of its inhabitants which are 
not prohibited by the constitution and which it would be competent for this Charter to set forth 
particularly or specifically, including all powers now or hereafter granted, and the specification herein of 
any particular powers shall not be held to be exclusive or any limitation of this general grant of powers.
ARTICLE II LEGISLATIVE DEPARTMENT
2.01
Composition, Eligibility, Election and Terms.
(a) There shall be a city council of five members elected by the voters of the city at largeby 
districts.  Any recall election or special election or appointment to fill a vacancy shall also be by 
district.  Following each decennial federal census, and at other such times as provided by law, 
the city council shall, by ordinance, adopt boundaries for all council districts so that all of the 
districts shall comply with state and federal law.    
(b) No person shall be eligible to hold office as a member of the city council or for election 
thereto unless he or she isthey are, and shall have been continuously for at least 30 days 
immediately preceding the appointment or final filing date for nomination papers for such 
office, a qualified elector and resident of the city, or of territory annexed to or consolidated with 
the city.
(c) The members of the city council shall be elected by the voters of the city at a general 
municipal election to be held in the year 2020 and every even-numbered year as follows:
(1) Two councilmembers shall be elected at the general municipal election held in the 
year 2020. They shall hold office for a term of four years, commencing on the first 
regular council meeting in the December immediately following the general municipal 
election until the general municipal election the fourth year thereafter.
(2) Three councilmembers shall be elected at the general municipal election held in the 
year 2022. They shall hold office for a term of four years, commencing on the first 
regular council meeting in the December immediately following the general municipal 
election until the general municipal election the fourth year thereafter.
